## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of position x) and possibly damping forces (functions of velocity v). Classical nonlinear oscillators include Duffing, Van der Pol, and other variants with polynomial or transcendental nonlinearities in x and v.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force with linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order polynomial restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (Duffing with position-dependent damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically driven linear oscillator)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force with saturation)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force, pendulum approximation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, hardening/softening spring behavior
- Position-dependent damping coefficient (x**2 * v term) → self-excited oscillations like Van der Pol
- Cubic velocity terms (v**3) → nonlinear energy dissipation, Rayleigh-type damping
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → large-amplitude pendulum-like dynamics
- Periodic forcing terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → externally driven oscillator with possible resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, conservative or dissipative
- Even powers of x (x**2) in restoring force → broken symmetry, asymmetric oscillations
- Product terms x*v → energy-exchange coupling between position and velocity degrees of freedom

$(c_0 v(c_1+v)\sin(x) + c_2 vx + c_3 x)/(c_1+v)$

Expanding: $c_0 v \sin(x) + \frac{c_2 vx + c_3 x}{c_1+v} = c_0 v \sin(x) + \frac{x(c_2 v + c_3)}{c_1+v}$

For the second term to equal a constant times x: $\frac{c_2 v + c_3}{c_1+v}$ must be constant in v. This requires $c_2 v + c_3 = k(c_1+v)$, so $c_2 = k$ and $c_3 = k c_1$. Then the expression becomes $c_0 v \sin(x) + c_2 x$. Setting $c_0 = -0.5837$, $c_2 = -1.8126$ works.

### Candidate 28:
$c_0\sin(c_1 x) + x(c_2 + c_3(c_4+v)^{c_5})$

Setting $c_1=1$: $c_0\sin(x) + x(c_2+c_3(c_4+v)^{c_5})$

For the v-dependent part to give v*sin(x)/x... it can't since sin(x) is separate from v. We'd need $c_3(c_4+v)^{c_5}$ to produce something with sin(x), but it doesn't depend on x.

Actually, we need $c_0\sin(x)$ to match $Av\sin(x)$, but $c_0$ is a constant, not v-dependent. And $x \cdot c_3(c_4+v)^{c_5}$ can't produce v*sin(x).

Candidate 28 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Setting $c_0=0$: $\frac{x(c_4 v+c_5)}{c_1+v} = kx$. No v*sin(x).

### Candidate 34:
$c_0 v\cos(c_1 t) + c_2 x + c_3 v^2 + c_4 x^3 + c_5\sin(c_6(c_7 x+c_8 v)+c_9)$

Setting $c_0=0, c_3=0, c_4=0$: $c_2 x + c_5\sin(c_6 c_7 x + c_6 c_8 v + c_9)$

We need $c_5\sin(c_6 c_7 x + c_6 c_8 v + c_9) = -0.5837 v\sin(x) - 1.8126 x - c_2 x$

$\sin(\alpha x + \beta v + \gamma)$ is a single sinusoidal function of a linear combination of x and v. This cannot equal $v\sin(x)$ which is a product. Not equivalent.

Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 35:

$= c_0\sin(x) + x(c_3 c_4 v + c_3 c_5 + c_4 v^2 + c_5 v)$

Need $c_4=0$ to eliminate $v^2$: $c_0\sin(x) + x(c_3 c_5 + c_5 v) = c_0\sin(x) + c_5 c_3 x + c_5 vx$

This gives $\sin(x)$ (not $v\sin(x)$) and $vx$ (not $v\sin(x)$). Can't match.
